## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillator dynamics (ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity), matching second-order dynamical systems x' = v, v' = f(x,v,t) used for linear/nonlinear harmonic oscillators (restoring forces, damping, and possible external driving). Time t may enter through parametric modulation or forcing terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- First-order state-space form: dx_dt = v, dv_dt = f(x, v, t) (canonical representation of a 2nd-order oscillator)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -c0 * x (restoring force proportional to displacement; small oscillations)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (external periodic forcing)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness; Mathieu-type structure)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x^3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear stiffness with quintic term: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x^3 - c2 * x^5 - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear restoring force)
- Pendulum (large-angle) model: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (trigonometric restoring torque; angular displacement as x)
- Piecewise/impact-like stiffening: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Abs(x) * x - c2 * v (odd restoring force with amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (drag proportional to speed squared)
- Coulomb (dry) friction oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * sign(v) (velocity-sign-dependent friction)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x^2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent self-excitation): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v^2) * v (nonlinear damping as a function of v)
- Liénard-type oscillator (general nonlinear damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * x^2) * v - c3 * x^3 (common template for many nonlinear oscillators)
- Potential-derived (conservative) oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x^3 + c2 * x^5) (dv_dt = -dU/dx with polynomial potential U(x))

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative vs dissipative: if dv_dt depends only on x (no v term), the system is energy-conserving; adding terms proportional to v (or nonlinear in v) introduces dissipation or self-excitation.
- Odd restoring-force symmetry: many physical springs/potentials yield dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -x - x^3, -sin(x)); even-in-x terms often indicate asymmetry or bias.
- Small-angle/weak-nonlinearity reduction: sin(c*x) ≈ c*x for small x, so models may transition from trigonometric to linear stiffness over limited amplitude data.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency: inclusion of x^3, x^5, or Abs(x)*x terms typically produces frequency that changes with oscillation amplitude (hardening/softening behavior).
- Damping identification via v structure: linear viscous damping appears as -c*v; aerodynamic damping as -c*v*Abs(v); dry friction as -c*sign(v).
- Limit-cycle indicators: terms like (c - x^2)*v (van der Pol) or (c - v^2)*v (Rayleigh) suggest negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, producing sustained oscillations.
- External forcing fingerprint: explicit periodic functions of t (cos/sin) in dv_dt imply driven response; sidebands/beat phenomena often motivate sums of harmonics in t.
- Parametric excitation fingerprint: stiffness multiplying x with time dependence (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x indicates modulation of natural frequency and possible parametric resonance.
- Non-smooth dynamics: Abs(·), sign(·), or piecewise terms often reflect contacts, impacts, backlash, or frictional stick-slip effects rather than smooth potentials.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO33)

GT: -c0*beta*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v - omega0**c3*(gamma*t + c4)*x - omega0**c5*x
Candidate formulas: 90

Let’s rewrite the Ground Truth (GT) in a simple expanded polynomial form.

### 1) Simplify the GT
GT numerical expression:
\[
-0.459914680311301\,v(1-v^2)\;-\;1.87329057400732\,v\;-\;2.49934616662645\,x(0.0579034145056311\,t+1)\;-\;2.49934616662645\,x
\]

Expand terms:

- Velocity part:
\[
-0.459914680311301\,v(1-v^2)= -0.459914680311301\,v + 0.459914680311301\,v^3
\]
So total \(v\) coefficient:
\[
(-0.459914680311301 - 1.87329057400732)= -2.333205254318621
\]
Thus velocity terms are:
\[
-2.333205254318621\,v + 0.459914680311301\,v^3
\]

- Position/time part:
\[
-2.49934616662645\,x(0.0579034145056311\,t+1)= -2.49934616662645\cdot 0.0579034145056311\,t x -2.49934616662645\,x
\]
Compute the \(t x\) coefficient:

```python
2.49934616662645*0.0579034145056311
```

This equals \(0.144715302...\) (approximately). So:
\[
-0.144715302\,t x -2.49934616662645\,x
\]
Then there is an additional \(-2.49934616662645 x\), giving total \(x\) coefficient:
\[
-4.9986923332529\,x
\]

So GT is exactly of the form:
\[
\boxed{GT = A\,x + B\,v + C\,t x + D\,v^3}
\]
with
- \(A=-4.9986923332529\)
- \(B=-2.333205254318621\)
- \(C\approx -0.144715302\)
- \(D=+0.459914680311301\)

No constants, no pure \(t\) term, no trig/log/exp, no absolute values, no denominators.

---

## 2) Check each candidate for possible equivalence

A candidate can match only if it can be reduced (by choosing parameters, often setting extra terms to 0) to exactly:
\[
c_x x + c_v v + c_{tx} t x + c_{v3} v^3
\]
with no other surviving dependence.

### Candidate 1
Has extra rational terms \(c4*t/(c5 t+c6)+c7/(c5 t+c6)\). Only removable by setting \(c4=c7=0\). Then becomes \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 t x + c3 v^3\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 2
Contains \(c2 x^{c3}\) and \(c5 t (c6+x)^{c7}\). To match GT, must remove the nonlinear-in-x term and the non-\(tx\) time term: set \(c2=0\) and \(c5=0\). Then \(c0 x + c1 v + c4 v^3\) (missing \(tx\) unless you rely on \(c5\), but \(c5\) term cannot become exactly \(t x\) without also introducing unwanted \(t\) constant unless \(c6=0,c7=1\). Actually if \(c6=0,c7=1\), then \(c5 t (x)=c5 t x\) works and introduces no extra term. So we can keep \(c5\neq0\) with \(c6=0,c7=1\). Then candidate becomes \(c0 x + c1 v + c5 t x + c4 v^3\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 3
Extra cosine term removable by \(c4=0\). Then becomes \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 t x + c3 v^3\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 4
Has additive sine term independent of \(x,v\); must set \(c2=0\). Remaining \(c0 x + c1 v + c5 t x + c6 v^3\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 5
Extra rational-in-x terms removable by \(c4=c7=0\). Then \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 t x + c3 v^3\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 6
Has extra \(c4 t + c5\). Must set \(c4=0,c5=0\). Then \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 t x + c3 v^3\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 7
Extra rational-in-v terms removable by \(c4=c7=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 8
Has \(x|x|\) (not equal to \(x\) globally) and \(t(c5+x)^{c6}\). Must set \(c2=0\). For the \(t(\cdot)\) term to become exactly \(t x\), choose \(c6=1,c5=0\), giving \(c4 t x\). Then candidate is \(c0 x + c1 v + c4 t x + c3 v^3\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 9
Has \(x\cos(c3 t)\) which cannot equal a linear combination of \(x\) and \(t x\) for all \(t\) unless coefficient is 0. So set \(c2=0\). Then as in candidate 2, choose \(c7=1,c6=0\) to make \(c5 t x\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 10
Extra \(\log(c5 t+1)\) must be removed by \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 11
Has log(v) term and \(t(c6+x)^{c7}\). Remove log by \(c3=0\). Make \(t x\) by \(c7=1,c6=0\). Then \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 v^3 + c5 t x\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 12
Has \(x^3\) term and \(t(c5+x)^{c6}\). Must set \(c1=0\). Make \(t x\) by \(c6=1,c5=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 13
Has \(t(c5+v)^{c6}\) which depends on \(v\) and \(t\) (not in GT). Must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 14
Has \(v/(c4+x)^{1/3}\) and \(t(c6+x)^{c7}\). Must set the fractional term \(c3=0\). Make \(t x\) by \(c7=1,c6=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 15
Has pure \(t\) term \(c1 t\); must set \(c1=0\). Then \(c0 x + c2 v + c4 t x + c3 v^3\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 16
Has \(c3 t^{c4}\) which cannot appear; set \(c3=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 17
Has \(v^{c3}\) plus \(t(c5+x)^{c6}\). Choose \(c3=3\) to get \(v^3\). Make \(t x\) by \(c6=1,c5=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 18
Has \(t(c5+x)^{c6}\). Make it \(t x\) by \(c6=1,c5=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 19
Has \(x\cos(t)\) which cannot be represented by \(x\) and \(t x\) globally; must set \(c2=0\). Then make \(t x\) via \(c6=1,c5=0\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 20
Everything divided by \((c1 t+c2)\). GT has no such denominator; cannot match for all \(t\) unless denominator is constant. Set \(c1=0\), denominator \(=c2\neq0\). Then expression becomes a linear combination of \(x,v,v^3,tx,tv,tv^3,t,1\) scaled by \(1/c2\). Set coefficients of unwanted terms \(tv,tv^3,t,1\) to 0: \(c6=c7=c8=c9=0\). Then it can match \(x,v,v^3,tx\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 21
Has \(c3 \exp(c4 t)\); must set \(c3=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 22
Has \(c4 \exp(c5\sin(\cdot))\) which cannot reduce to polynomial unless \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 23
Has sine(log(|v|)) term; must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 24
Has \(x^{c3}\) and rational-in-t terms. To match: set \(c2=0\) (remove \(x^{c3}\)) and set \(c5=c8=0\) (remove rational terms). Then left with \(c0 x + c1 v + c4 v^3\) (missing \(tx\) and no other way to create it). So **not matchable**.

### Candidate 25
Has \(\sin(c3 x+c4)\) (non-polynomial in x); must set \(c2=0\). Then polynomial form with \(t x\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 26
Has \(x|x|\) and rational-in-t terms. Must set \(c2=0\) and \(c4=c7=0\). Then only \(x,v,v^3\) (no \(tx\)). So **not matchable**.

### Candidate 27
Has \(x\cos(c3 t)\) and rational-in-t terms. Must set those to 0: \(c2=0\), \(c5=0\), \(c8=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 28
Has \(\sin(c3 v+c4)\); must set \(c2=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 29
Has cosine(log(exp(v))) term; must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

Has log(v) and rational-in-t. Must set \(c3=0\) and \(c5=c8=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 31
Has rational-in-t terms; set \(c4=c7=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 32
Has \(v/(c5 x+c6)\) and rational term; must set \(c4=c7=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

Has \(x^3\) and rational-in-t. Set \(c1=0\), \(c4=c7=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 34
Has extra \(c4 v + c5\). Constant must be 0: \(c5=0\). The extra \(v\) can be absorbed into \(c1 v\) by redefining \(c1\). So effectively polynomial form. **Matchable.**

Has extra constant \(c4\); set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

Has extra \(c4 x + c5\). Combine \(x\) terms; set \(c5=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 45
Like 20 but includes an extra \(v/(den)\) term; still can set denominator constant by \(c1=0\). Then set unwanted terms to 0 (e.g., \(c6=c7=c9=0\)) and merge the two \(v\) terms (from \(c3\) and \(c8\)). Can keep \(x,v,v^3,tx\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 49
Has \(c4 v^{c5} e^{c6 t}\) which cannot appear; must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 50
Has \(c4 v (c5+t)^{c6}\) (time-v coupling not in GT); must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 51
Has \(c4 x (c5+t)^{c6}\). This could equal \(t x\) only if \((c5+t)^{c6}\) is proportional to \(t\) for all \(t\), which is impossible as a pure power shift (unless you allow restricting domain, which we do not). So must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form remains and still has \(tx\) already via \(c2 t x\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 52
Has \(x\cos(\cdot)\) terms; cannot become linear \(x\) and \(tx\) globally unless those coefficients are 0: set \(c2=0,c5=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 53
Has \(v^{c4}\) plus \(v^3\). You can set \(c2=0\) to remove \(v^{c4}\), leaving polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 54
Has \(x\cos(t)\) and \(x\sin(\cdot)\); must set \(c2=0,c4=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 55
Has \(x^{c3}\) and \(x\sin(\cdot)\); must set \(c2=0,c5=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 57

### Candidate 58
Has \(x^{c3}\) and \(x(c6+t)^{c7}\) (not equal to \(tx\) globally). Best is set \(c2=0,c5=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 59

### Candidate 60

### Candidate 63
Has extra \(x^{c5}\sin(\cdot)\); set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 64
Has \(v^{c5}x^{c6}\); must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 66
Has \(x\cos(t)\) and \(x(c5+t)^{c6}\). Must set both extra x-time nonlinear terms to 0: \(c2=0,c4=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 67
Has \(x|x|\) and \(x(c5+t)^{c6}\). Must set \(c2=0,c4=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 68
Has \(x|x|\) which cannot be in GT; must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 69
Has fractional term and \(x(c6+t)^{c7}\). Must set \(c3=0\). The remaining \(x(c6+t)^{c7}\) cannot equal \(tx\) globally, so must set \(c5=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 70
Has \(x\cos(c3 t)\) and \(x(c6+t)^{c7}\). Must set both to 0: \(c2=0,c5=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 71
Has \(x\cos(c5 t)\); must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 72
Has \(x|x|\) and \(x^{c5}\sin(\cdot)\). Must set \(c2=0,c4=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 73
Has \(\log(c5 x+1)\); must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 74
Is effectively \((c0+c1)x + c2 v + c4 t x + c3 v^3\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 75
Has \(x,v,v^3,tx\) (since \(c3 v^3\)) plus extra \(c3 v\) term? Actually it has both \(c1 v\) and \(c3 v\) (via \(c3*v\) in formula): those combine. So polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 76
Exactly \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 t x + c3 v^3\). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 77
Has \(v^{c3}\) and \(x(c5+t)^{c6}\) (not \(tx\)). You can set \(c4=0\) to remove the bad x-time term, but then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 78
Has \(x,v,tx\) and two \(v^3\) terms that combine. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 79
Has \(x(v)\)-coupled term \(t x\) plus \(x(c5+v)^{c6}\) which must be removed: set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 80
Has \(v(c5+x)^{c6}\) coupling; must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 81
Has \(v x^2\) term not in GT; must set \(c3=0\). Then polynomial form (it already has \(tx\) and \(v^3\)). **Matchable.**

### Candidate 82
Has \(v|v|\) which is not equal to \(v^3\) globally; must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 83
Has \(v/\sqrt{c5+v^2}\) non-polynomial; must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 84
Has log(v) and \(x(c6+t)^{c7}\). Must set log term \(c3=0\). The \(x(c6+t)^{c7}\) cannot become \(tx\) globally, so must set \(c5=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 85
Has \(\log(c5 v+1)\); must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 86
Has \(x^5\); must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 87
Has \(x^3\) and \(x(c5+t)^{c6}\). Must set \(c1=0\) and \(c4=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 88
Has \(x^3\); must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

### Candidate 89
Has \(x^3\) and \(x^{c5} e^{c6 t}\). Must set \(c1=0\) and \(c4=0\). Then no \(tx\). **Not matchable.**

### Candidate 90
Has \(e^{c5 v}\log(|x|)\) term; must set \(c4=0\). Then polynomial form. **Matchable.**

## 3) Conclusion and explicit matching example
Since many candidates reduce exactly to \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 t x + c3 v^3\), and GT is exactly of that form, a match exists.

For example Candidate 76 matches by choosing:
- \(c0 = -4.9986923332529\)
- \(c1 = -2.333205254318621\)
- \(c2 \approx -0.144715302\)
- \(c3 = 0.459914680311301\)

Therefore at least one candidate can be made identical to GT.
